  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_913d3b60-b4f8-497b-badf-9feb08c1c7fd'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=october-is-spooky">october-is-spooky</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229281088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9002240051460464707"><br/>if anyone popped into my RA group looking for a book that was "not well-written, consistent, or plausible," i could hand them this book with full confidence.<br/><br/>and i feel bad for saying that, i do. this book means well, you can tell. the author dedicated it to his best friend erin. that's cute, right? but about thirty pages in, i started getting concerned that this was another YA book actually written by a teen author. i am not going to have another <i>truancy</i> experience, thank you very much. but no, </span>
  <span id="freeText9002240051460464707" style="display:none"><br />if anyone popped into my RA group looking for a book that was "not well-written, consistent, or plausible," i could hand them this book with full confidence.<br /><br />and i feel bad for saying that, i do. this book means well, you can tell. the author dedicated it to his best friend erin. that's cute, right? but about thirty pages in, i started getting concerned that this was another YA book actually written by a teen author. i am not going to have another <i>truancy</i> experience, thank you very much. but no, not a teen, just the brother of dan wells, who i still have yet to read, but seems like a really nice guy. <br /><br />so this is why i feel bad for hating on this book, because the brother of the author has always been nice when he has come in. that makes perfect sense, right? also, i write my least convincing book reports when i am ill. but these are the cards we were dealt today. <br /><br />so, seventeen-year-old benson fisher applies for a boarding-school scholarship program in order to get out of the foster-care system cycle he has been swirling around inside for years.he gets it - yayyy - and flies off to new mexico to settle into his new school and meet his new classmates. but oh no! where are the teachers? where are the adult cafeteria and maintenance workers? why are all the children shouting? so, basically - this is a school in which all the duties of the school are performed by the students themselves. please hold your questions until the end. so there are three groups, groups that have formed out of necessity, after some unpleasantness in the past, when the students had been just fending for themselves. and by unpleasantness, i mean many many deaths. this being YA fiction, the groups have suitably goofy names: the society- who play by the rules, havoc - who wear thuglife pendants and like to fight, and the variants - who would like to escape, but are very pragmatic and would like a color-coded escape plan first, please. for safety's sake. (which group do you think benson aligns himself with? i give you a hint and point you towards the title of the book) so, each of these groups perform certain functions in the school, based on agreed-upon and bidded-for contracts. havoc is in charge of food and groundskeeping, society handles admin, nursing, teaching, variants clean up the trash, but all are ruled by a tv screen that depicts an adult face giving out daily punishments, after reviewing the tapes culled from the numerous video cameras and microphones all around the school. and if you get detention, you never come back.... shhhh - questions at the end, please!the lessons are arbitrary lectures on aesthetics or field surveying, and they play a lot of paintball, and points are accrued all around so they can buy clothing and other gear, but never.... their freeeeeedom. so it is shades of <i>ender's game</i>, shades of <i>lord of the flies</i>, shades of any other of the recent batch of YA dystopia where kids form little white gangs and adhere to bizarre group standards in order to show that they are independently minded freethinkers - hey! hands down! and there are ample excuses as to why the kids were chosen, why they can't just call for help or use the internet, or escape over the wall, why they don't just... stop. <br /><br />okay - now time for questions.<br /><br />okay, so i just wrote out a string of like 20 questions, but ended up deleting them all because they would probably be too spoilery, for those of you who are interested in reading this, despite my warnings. because it still looks like a book i <i>should</i> like. greg brought it to me at work, saying just that, "this looks like a book you would read." and i did read it. and it was bad. and i am glad i borrowed it rather than buying it, because i was about to buy it, actually. but now i can bring it back. and maybe the person who reads it next will love it, and i would be pleased to hear it. i just hate it when i dislike a book that looks like it means well. it tried, right? especially when it went nuts there at the end and decided to try something "new," and everyone went "whaaaaa??" and then laffed. baffling. truly baffling.<br /><br />but i will allow this one question - why are YA novels always structured this way, where characters huddle together in like-minded groups instead of utilizing the strengths of all participants? does no one see how this limits the resources? it is a structure that only works if the book is well-written enough to overcome its own inherent silliness. <i>divergent</i> was, i thought, fantastic, even though it had a lot of its own foolishness to overcome. this one tripped over its own foolishness, and then stumbled down a hill, caught on fire, and then just smoldered there.in a not-very-sexy way.<br /><br />now i am going back to bed. i wouldn't say this book <i>gave</i> me this surely-fatal illness, but i'm also not ruling it out.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9002240051460464707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_234127157" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/234127157" />
    <a title="Sue" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6298636-sue"><img alt="Sue" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/234127157?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue" href="/user/show/6298636-sue">Sue</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer234127157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17720006343115269504">Simple words: BLOODY BRILLIANT!!!<br/><br/>I've read so much of YA, and from the first page, everything is so predictable, you have an idea of the direction and what will happen at the end. Even the Dystopian novels, the main problem is X and you obviously know that the MC will survive.<br/><br/>But THIS. I could not for one second predict where this would go and I'm excellent at predicting what's next. <br/><br/>The writing served its purpose, I didn't have to skim over anything. You know how in novels sometimes the prose i</span>
  <span id="freeText17720006343115269504" style="display:none">Simple words: BLOODY BRILLIANT!!!<br /><br />I've read so much of YA, and from the first page, everything is so predictable, you have an idea of the direction and what will happen at the end. Even the Dystopian novels, the main problem is X and you obviously know that the MC will survive.<br /><br />But THIS. I could not for one second predict where this would go and I'm excellent at predicting what's next. <br /><br />The writing served its purpose, I didn't have to skim over anything. You know how in novels sometimes the prose is striking and beautiful and the descriptions so vivid? And there's a bunch of symbols that give deep meaning and yada yada yada. There's none of that in this.<br /><br />Because really, if you're the narrator writing and it's in first person, do you really go on and describe the sky's purple hues and the symbolism of a bird over your head? And then you map out the skies as say how thick the clouds are so it must be raining and you go all philosophical? Yeah, screw that. Be real and tell it like it is, not overly-descriptive, not too sparse, just a need-to-know basis and the narrative is genuine in following the character's train of thought. <br /><br />The action was good, the pace was fast and most of the time you really just had to wonder what will happen next. I honestly couldn't put the book down even with a gun to my head. I just had to know what to know what will happen.<br /><br />The characters are definitely interesting and our MC isn't overly superficially brilliant. He isn't someone who comes into the school and manages to overcome everything with ease like a supergod character and is armed with some ridiculously helpful skill. Benson is not one of those characters when in a hard situation amazingly shows his awesomeness with skills like super combat, gun expertise and survival skills even though the character is only a teen. A lot of what he learned is from TV, which is genuine given all the CSI watching these days. He's not one of those brilliant charismatic characters who manages to unite and bring everyone on his side either. <br /><br />I also applaud the book in no plot holes that I've picked up on. i hate it when scenarios are implausible. Like that one main character doesn't get caught even though the streets are patrolled, yeah right. For once the MC actually keeps up with what's going on like a real reader. You know how sometimes in books the villain or something is so glaringly obvious and yet the character is still dumb when readers have already figured it out halfway and the characters haven't? None of that here. I love how he instantly picks up on every nuance, how we have a character who is smart enough to ask questions instead of mulling over it and only having that one moment where he pieces everything together. It's a step-by-step process, not some eureka moment. It's just so refreshing to have a character who is intelligent and who realises thing fast enough so there can be real action and events in the novel and move things along.<br /><br />I'm desperately waiting for the sequel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17720006343115269504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_228706577" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228706577" />
    <a title="Lucy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3813315-lucy"><img alt="Lucy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307662921p2/3813315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228706577?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy" href="/user/show/3813315-lucy">Lucy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=milking-a-money-cow">milking-a-money-cow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=make-room-for-that-sequel">make-room-for-that-sequel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=blah-world-building">blah-world-building</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3813315-lucy?shelf=book-with-no-ending">book-with-no-ending</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228706577" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14799203228841075606">So my dog does this cute thing sometimes where he chases down a toy or ball with such intensity that he sometimes crashes into walls and furniture. After he does this he looks up at me with an expression on his face that I'd like to catch on camera without deliberately letting him get a concussion. It's a cross between 'where the fuck did that come from' and 'how did I get here again' because you see he's forgotten he was chasing a ball in the surprise of his encounter.<br/><br/>This book put that express</span>
  <span id="freeText14799203228841075606" style="display:none">So my dog does this cute thing sometimes where he chases down a toy or ball with such intensity that he sometimes crashes into walls and furniture. After he does this he looks up at me with an expression on his face that I'd like to catch on camera without deliberately letting him get a concussion. It's a cross between 'where the fuck did that come from' and 'how did I get here again' because you see he's forgotten he was chasing a ball in the surprise of his encounter.<br /><br />This book put that expression on my face a lot. Sometimes being surprised and a little confused can make for an amazing book if the technique is right... the technique was not spot on here. The surprises felt really random. I feel like telling everyone where the book got weird, but it's a pretty big spoiler and you never get much more information about it beyond that one fact.<br /><br />The writing was simplistic. It kind of reminded me of the first two Percy Jackson books, which are more on the middle school end of the YA swimming pool. It's all functional, but it's not a style that allows you to feel fully emerged in the main character or even the story. There's always a slight sense of detachment that kept me from really connecting to or sympathizing with the main character's plights.<br /><br />Benson Fisher, the main character, was also exceedingly difficult to like. He does a lot of stupid shit without thinking it through. He takes big gambles with the school's social order and structure without fully thinking about what will happen even though he has all the necessary information to realize he could be making a big mistake. As a reader I certainly knew he was fucking up everyone's lives. Let's see, the last time people did what he was doing... there were gang wars that resulted in student on student murder several times over, but he goes for it, tells no one, and then takes a nap after instead of bracing himself for the fall out. Smart. See, YA Paranormal Romance heroines aren't the only unlikeable fools out there.<br /><br />The end of the book pissed me off. There is no ending. This series seems to be one of those series where the books aren't individual stories building into a whole. I say seems because this is only book one, but this book ended abruptly without closing any major story archs. The author opens more for the next book, but he misses a big step in reader satisfaction by leaving almost every major plot open from this book.<br /><br />I'd recommend this to really young adults. 11-14 or maybe 15, boys in particular might like it more. It's got a fair bit of action, a male lead, and they tend to be more forgiving of simplistic writing. I don't think adult YA fans will find anything here for themselves.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14799203228841075606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer616760905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5592770612573046402">Variant is like The Maze Runner. (And it's kinda awkward that James Dashner blurbed this book.) I mean both has the same set-up where teens are trapped in a secluded, unknown place and don't know any idea why they are there. But both are still different in many aspects, anyway. I still like Maze Runner (just the first book, not its sequels, EW!) more than this book .<br/><br/>In my honest opinion, there weren't much happened in the book until Benson, the main character, discovered something he didn't expe</span>
  <span id="freeText5592770612573046402" style="display:none">Variant is like The Maze Runner. (And it's kinda awkward that James Dashner blurbed this book.) I mean both has the same set-up where teens are trapped in a secluded, unknown place and don't know any idea why they are there. But both are still different in many aspects, anyway. I still like Maze Runner (just the first book, not its sequels, EW!) more than this book .<br /><br />In my honest opinion, there weren't much happened in the book until Benson, the main character, discovered something he didn't expect. The good thing was Variant is engrossingly readable and the mystery will drive you insane or just curious to know what's the mystery behind this fucking academy. <br /><br />Like I said, there weren't much happened but I seriously love the paintball scenes (heh). I don't know exactly why but I enjoyed reading those. And the rest is history. Blech. Because, really, nothing happened. Ugh.<br /><br />In terms of characters, they are mostly one dimensional. I can't connect with them and don't really care about them. The back stories of some characters are trying-hard and felt like as fillers. But, I thought it was fine since the mystery and anticipation compensate for it. Which is the main reason I still gave it 3 stars.</span>

<div id="review_238152748" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238152748" />
    <a title="Margot" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3800614-margot"><img alt="Margot" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364517784p2/3800614.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/238152748?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margot" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margot" href="/user/show/3800614-margot">Margot</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062093516" href="/book/show/11518299-variant">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3800614-margot?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3800614-margot?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3800614-margot?shelf=autumn-2011">autumn-2011</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238152748" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5696786044540274744">I can't think of a single reason why I shouldn't give this a five-star rating. I loved everything about it. <br/><br/>First of all, <i>Variant</i> is one original little book. Yeah, everyone says the same about all the books they read, but I definitely found Variant refreshing and unique. And I really enjoyed Benson's voice. <br/><br/><i>Variant</i> hooked me right in since the very beginning—I couldn't put it down. I found it original, thrilling, compelling, and so easy to read. Interesting from the first page to the very last </span>
  <span id="freeText5696786044540274744" style="display:none">I can't think of a single reason why I shouldn't give this a five-star rating. I loved everything about it. <br /><br />First of all, <i>Variant</i> is one original little book. Yeah, everyone says the same about all the books they read, but I definitely found Variant refreshing and unique. And I really enjoyed Benson's voice. <br /><br /><i>Variant</i> hooked me right in since the very beginning—I couldn't put it down. I found it original, thrilling, compelling, and so easy to read. Interesting from the first page to the very last one, where it left us with a cliffhanger. <br /><br />There were parts where my heart was pounding in anticipation, and I was pretty much biting my nails—I couldn't read fast enough—because just when I thought he—and I—had something figured out, surprising little twists happened. <br /><br />It was nice to read a good YA book that had an unpredictable plot for a change. I wanted something different and this absolutely delivered. I cannot wait for the sequel. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5696786044540274744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_224558243" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/224558243" />
    <a title="Reynje" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje"><img alt="Reynje" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473722441p2/5590906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/224558243?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynje" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynje" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje">Reynje</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer224558243" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14308782524860560962"><br/>Well, the joke is on me apparently.<br/> <br/>As I was racing towards the end of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10433900.Variant' title='Variant by Robison Wells' rel='nofollow noopener'>Variant</a> it became very clear that the number of pages I had left to read were not going to be adequate to address the plethora of unanswered questions I had. My rising mental chorus of <i>”But what about...? But why...? How....?</i> smacked straight into a four word brick wall: <b>End of Book One.</b><br/> <br/>I really thought this was a standalone book. Ha ha.<br/> <br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10433900.Variant' title='Variant by Robison Wells' rel='nofollow noopener'>Variant</a> is a fast-paced, fairly gripping read that slaps you with quite a doozy of a cli</span>
  <span id="freeText14308782524860560962" style="display:none"><br />Well, the joke is on me apparently.<br /> <br />As I was racing towards the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10433900.Variant" title="Variant by Robison Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">Variant</a> it became very clear that the number of pages I had left to read were not going to be adequate to address the plethora of unanswered questions I had. My rising mental chorus of <i>”But what about...? But why...? How....?</i> smacked straight into a four word brick wall: <b>End of Book One.</b><br /> <br />I really thought this was a standalone book. Ha ha.<br /> <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10433900.Variant" title="Variant by Robison Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">Variant</a> is a fast-paced, fairly gripping read that slaps you with quite a doozy of a cliffhanger on the last page. It’s told through the first-person perspective of seventeen-year old Benson Fisher, who applies for and receives a scholarship to Maxfield Academy, thinking this will be a relief from a life spent in a series of foster homes. Of course, all is not what it seems.<br /> <br />There are no adults at Maxfield, just intense video camera monitoring and four rules: no “violent” fights, no sex, no refusing punishment and no trying to escape. Breaking the rules results in detention, and no one returns from detention. <br /><br />Sometime prior to Benson’s arrival, the students of Maxfield had been getting their Lord of the Flies on in an all out intra-school war (really, what is it with me and books about kids beating the heck out of each other?). A tenuous truce between the three “gangs” (Havoc, Society and Variant) has brought a kind of precarious order to life in the Academy. So what exactly is going on? Is this a prison? Are they unwitting lab rats in a cage? And who is behind the sinister rules and punishments of Maxfield?<br /> <br />It’s a chilling premise and the for the most part, I think, well done. Wells’ keeps a tight rein on the tension and it builds rapidly, making this a fast-paced read. There’s definitely an unsettling atmosphere of paranoia about the whole claustrophobic set up, especially through Benson’s eyes as the newcomer. Comparing his viewpoint with that of the students who accept their strange lives with a type of <i>“it’s this or die”</i> resignation, is quite effective. The power play – both psychological and outright physical - between the different factions of students is disturbing and keeps the story compelling.<br /><br />As a heavily plot driven story, the characterisation and development of relationships felt a bit thinner than what I usually enjoy. The primary focus here is on Benson attempting to figure out what’s going on and plotting escape, although he does form some tentative bonds with some students. <br /><br />The writing is brisk and quite business-like, which suits the pace and the urgency of Benson’s situation. (After all, this is not really a story to linger over, but one that almost forces you to race through). The sharp twists throughout, and particularly towards the end, are neatly orchestrated and pack enough shock value to consistently hold attention. <br /><br />And the ending? Well, all I’ll say is that Variant raises more questions than it answers. <br /><br /><br />And beware if you’re not a fan of severe cliffhangers :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14308782524860560962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5277716-sasha?shelf=dystopian-postapocalyptic">dystopian-postapocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5277716-sasha?shelf=harpercollins">harpercollins</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174341938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10678663038303615972">This is the story of Benson Fisher and how he settles into his new life at Maxfield Academy, where there are no teachers, no grades, and only 4 rules. The school is split into three different "gangs" and these gangs have come to an agreement that will keep them at peace..most of the time. And then Benson comes across the school's real secret..so, what will he do with this information and what will the consequences of his actions be?<br/><br/>This book was a thriller right from the beginning. Within the fi</span>
  <span id="freeText10678663038303615972" style="display:none">This is the story of Benson Fisher and how he settles into his new life at Maxfield Academy, where there are no teachers, no grades, and only 4 rules. The school is split into three different "gangs" and these gangs have come to an agreement that will keep them at peace..most of the time. And then Benson comes across the school's real secret..so, what will he do with this information and what will the consequences of his actions be?<br /><br />This book was a thriller right from the beginning. Within the first 15 pages or so, I was already asking myself TONS of questions about the school - about the kids - about EVERYTHING. I found myself just as scared/angry as Benson was about the whole situation. I think that's one of the things that made this book so good for me - I really, truly connected with the characters. I felt like I was actually there, right along side Benson.<br /><br />Variant was such a unique take on the idea of a Dystopian society and the ending left me begging for more. (I literally tweeted at Mr. Wells asking him if he had already written the second book.) I don't know where this series is heading, but this guessing-game is very refreshing for me.<br /><br />Every so often, a book comes along that I would recommend for anyone and everyone. This is one of those books. I can't think of anyone who wouldn't like this thrilling, action-packed story - including teenage boys, who are very hard to pick out a book for.<br /><br />You'll especially like this book if you enjoyed The Maze Runner by James Dashner.</span>

Gracious.               <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=galleys">galleys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191403909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3820855943210657862">4ish stars (yes I'm a little wishy-washy on this point)<br/><br/>Variant is one of those books that's hard to review. (Yes I know I say that a lot!).<br/><br/>It's a book with a First Half. Then a Second Half. And I want to judge them separately. Because by the end I couldn't put the book down, almost finishing it in a loud chinese restaurant because I was that engaged. But as much as I enjoyed the second half, I can't ignore the first half of the book.<br/><br/>The first half I kinda wanted to smack the main character. Have</span>
  <span id="freeText3820855943210657862" style="display:none">4ish stars (yes I'm a little wishy-washy on this point)<br /><br />Variant is one of those books that's hard to review. (Yes I know I say that a lot!).<br /><br />It's a book with a First Half. Then a Second Half. And I want to judge them separately. Because by the end I couldn't put the book down, almost finishing it in a loud chinese restaurant because I was that engaged. But as much as I enjoyed the second half, I can't ignore the first half of the book.<br /><br />The first half I kinda wanted to smack the main character. Have you heard that famous Albert Einstein quote? "The definition of insanity is doing the same thing over and over and expecting different results." For me that's the first half of this book. Benson has only one thing on his mind. And it's something he SHOULD have on his mind. Only problem is that Benson has a bad case of the "doesn't stop and think."<br /><br /><i>"No one talked about escape. I tried to bring up the subject once, but it died out fairly quickly."</i><br /> Benson my friend, I hate to tell you this but you did not bring it up once. I searched on my Kindle. The word escape appears 76 times. You might have been a wee bit obsessed.<br /><br />BUT then comes the second half where everything changed. And I could not put the book down. The problem? I can't actually TELL you much about the second half without ruining the nicely done twist.<br /><br />When we first meet Benson (which FYI had me thinking of Law &amp; Order SVU every time they said his name) he's on his way to Maxfield Academy. He thinks a scholarship to an elite private school is his escape from the foster system. But Maxfield Academy is not what he thinks. It's not a wonderful opportunity, it's more like a prison than school. Instead he's trapped behind bullet proof glass and barbed wire fences, with no adults. The school is controlled by 3 different gangs and breaking a rule equals detention and detention equals death. It's not exactly the bright future Benson hopes for .<br /><br />I feel like I should be able to sympathize with Benson. Maxfield Academy is horrible and it does suck. He's RIGHT about pretty much everything. But his approach is wrong. He is single-mindly obsessed with escape. He's practically banging his head against the wall hoping to knock a stone loose. I spent the first half of the book wanting to shout at him. "QUIT RUNNING HEADLONG INTO DANGER! STOP AND THINK!!!!!" Benson is not much of a thinker, at least not at first.<br /><br />But then about halfway through the book, just when Benson is finally calming down, falling for a girl and starting to get complacent, everything suddenly changes. Like BOOM I'm going to be a different book now. Like me better now? As a matter of fact yes I do like you better. You should have dyed your hair this color pages ago, does wonders for your pacing! Honestly the second half of this book made me question my opinion of the first. "Surely it can't be that annoying Cassi? Look how much you like it now!" So I suppose there's always the chance I was in a bad mood when I read the first half. I don't think so, but you never know.<br /><br />Suddenly you can't trust anyone. Benson finally stops running in circles and starts thinking strategically. For me that's when the book gets good. When he stops banging his head against the proverbial wall and starts planning. Finally he's trying to figure out the big mystery of the school and tries to come up with a feasible escape plan (whereas his plan before was just jump the wall and hope not to die). This gives the reader the opportunity to follow his investigation and put the pieces of the puzzle together along with Benson.<br /><br />Then ending is twisty, leaving the reader on a cliffhanger that made me say "HUH". I re-read the passage and I was still confused, but it was a good confusion (I was a Lost fan, clearly I have a thing for confusing cliffhangers). The ending left me curious enough that I want to read book 2.<br /><br />This book has a Dystopian-vibe without actually being a Dystopia. It's a little bit sci-fi, a little bit thriller and a little bit something else that I can't place my finger on. But overall I liked it. The first portion may be a 3, but the last part is solidly 4+. In fictional math that equals a 4 star review for me.<br /><br />So even though Benson is a little obnoxious at the beginning of the book, bear with him because he gets smarter. There's an interesting mystery, a creepy school and life or death stakes. The book is clearly meant to be part of a series (trilogy is my guess) because you don't get all the answers in this book. Assuming that the new and improved Benson plans to make an appearance in the next book I want to continue this series. And the cliffhanger better be worth it! Not just a shark with a random dharma logo!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3820855943210657862" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_176376546" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/176376546" />
    <a title="Cory" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4942446-cory"><img alt="Cory" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423019739p2/4942446.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/176376546?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cory" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cory" href="/user/show/4942446-cory">Cory</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer176376546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1714087360811713262">More reviews @ <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://antidrugreads.blogspot.com'>http://antidrugreads.blogspot.com</a><br/><br/>If I were to just call Variant unpredictable, that would be an undoubtable understatement. By the end of the book, my mind was completely blown. The places I assumed or expected this story to go throughout my reading, proved to be wrong every single time.<br/><br/>"Trust no one" is the perfect tag line for Robison Wells's creation. Benson, the protagonist, thinks he just got a scholarship to an upper class prep school, but boy is he wrong. What he gets in re</span>
  <span id="freeText1714087360811713262" style="display:none">More reviews @ <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://antidrugreads.blogspot.com">http://antidrugreads.blogspot.com</a><br /><br />If I were to just call Variant unpredictable, that would be an undoubtable understatement. By the end of the book, my mind was completely blown. The places I assumed or expected this story to go throughout my reading, proved to be wrong every single time.<br /><br />"Trust no one" is the perfect tag line for Robison Wells's creation. Benson, the protagonist, thinks he just got a scholarship to an upper class prep school, but boy is he wrong. What he gets in reality, is a one way ticket to a prison. This prison isn't much different from a regular prep school though- Students, dorms, and classes. The differences are that there are no adults, walls and locked doors prohibit escape, and calls home are replaced with death threats. All the kids are being treated like lab rats. Some of the student go along with what is happening, while others like Benson aren't as compliant. This is where the story takes off. Numerous situations at the "school" cause Benson to plot an intricate escape and trust no one.<br /><br />Benson's first person narration is quite refreshing. The YA genre is dominated by female narrators, so I jumped at the chance to read Variant. Benson is an extremely determined fellow. Fear and rationality always seem to take back seat whenever his mind is set, no matter the danger. I found it to be a respectable trait, especially since it made for a suspenseful story!<br /><br />Robison Wells did a phenomenal job with creating a unique story in a popular genre. His dystopian world is controlled, and has the potential of going in multiple different directions. I'm having a hard time writing this review, because I don't want to risk spoiling anything. Everyone deserves to be as shocked as I was after reading all the rattling scenarios.<br /><br />I know Variant doesn't come out till the first of October, but I just had to read and post my review of it. I am not one who can handle anticipation well. Variant kept me guessing till the very end, and then left me dangling off a cliff. Now to the best of my ability, I will wait anxiously for the second book in the series. *eyes twitching*</span>
  <a data-text-id="1714087360811713262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4544076-erin-bowman?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150601240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2567627446670741078">I’ve heard this book described as a “Lord of the Flies” set at boarding school. Um, yeah. That sounds awesome. And it is. From the second Benson sets foot within the grounds of Maxfield Academy – which happens within the first several pages, mind you – things are intense. Examples: there are no teachers, students have split into gangs, cameras watch everything, everywhere, and no one ever leaves the campus. This book is fast paced and near impossible to put down. Benson is not a perfect person, </span>
  <span id="freeText2567627446670741078" style="display:none">I’ve heard this book described as a “Lord of the Flies” set at boarding school. Um, yeah. That sounds awesome. And it is. From the second Benson sets foot within the grounds of Maxfield Academy – which happens within the first several pages, mind you – things are intense. Examples: there are no teachers, students have split into gangs, cameras watch everything, everywhere, and no one ever leaves the campus. This book is fast paced and near impossible to put down. Benson is not a perfect person, but he has a good heart. He tries to do the right thing in the upside-down world into which he is thrown. He is on a constant lookout for answers and while that narrow vision sometimes had me pulling at my hair, he is a fabulous reluctant hero.<br /><br />And then of course, there’s the twists. This book is FULL of them. Every time I thought I’d figured something out, Wells threw another curve ball at me. And the ending. Oh boy, the ending. I can’t say much else without spoiling things. Just get your hands on this.<br /><br />Originally reviewed <a href="http://www.embowman.com/2011/reading-july/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a><br />NOTE: This review is based on an ARC</span>
  <a data-text-id="2567627446670741078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2532303266933316657">VARIANT is the kind of book you race through, unable to stop even though you're eyes are tired and it's late at night. Wells has created a compelling closed society, with characters that live and breathe on the page. <br/><br/>Not really a dystopian, but with the chills and twists of a boarding school that creates a dystopian-esque atmosphere. <br/><br/>One of the best reads of 2011 for me. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/397225984?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer397225984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8192650018464603787">I don't know what to think of this book. Throughout the entire book I was reminded of the Maze Runner by James Dashner, except I loved that series! This book was just strange to me. I found the believability aspect of it to be extremely lacking. I just didn't believe these kids would conform to a school like this rather than trying to get out. I didn't believe the circumstances they were given and when we found out the big secret, I didn't even believe the explanation we were given. None of it m</span>
  <span id="freeText8192650018464603787" style="display:none">I don't know what to think of this book. Throughout the entire book I was reminded of the Maze Runner by James Dashner, except I loved that series! This book was just strange to me. I found the believability aspect of it to be extremely lacking. I just didn't believe these kids would conform to a school like this rather than trying to get out. I didn't believe the circumstances they were given and when we found out the big secret, I didn't even believe the explanation we were given. None of it made sense. I don't want to give spoilers so I can't go into too much detail, I just didn't get it. Maybe it was because I kept thinking of the Maze Runner... but the scenario in those books by Mr. Dashner WERE believable... those kids in the glade were always looking for an out, they never just accepted their circumstances without questioning everything. The kids at Maxfield Academy were just mindless and boring after the kids in the glade. <br /><br />As I stated, maybe it was wrong of me to compare the books, but it was hard not to. The situations were a lot alike to me. I may read the next book to see what happens, but I'm glad I didn't buy this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8192650018464603787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1024524906" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1024524906" />
    <a title="Joe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/406752-joe"><img alt="Joe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497186280p2/406752.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1024524906?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joe" href="/user/show/406752-joe">Joe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/406752-joe?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/406752-joe?shelf=borrowed-library">borrowed-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/406752-joe?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1024524906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7968389939081960806"><i>Variant</i> is the perfect name for this book, because it is, itself, a variation of...<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Lord of the Flies</i>
</b> <br/>In Golding's classic, which has its fair share of detractors, children and teenagers are thrust into a truly upsetting situation that supplies a chilling context for Golding to explore mob mentality, primal urges, and the tightrope walk of animal instinct and human compassion.<br/><br/>Wells attempts to expand this theme by putting teenagers in a boarding school with no teachers and a sloppily construc</span>
  <span id="freeText7968389939081960806" style="display:none"><i>Variant</i> is the perfect name for this book, because it is, itself, a variation of...<br><br><b>
  <i>Lord of the Flies</i>
</b> <br>In Golding's classic, which has its fair share of detractors, children and teenagers are thrust into a truly upsetting situation that supplies a chilling context for Golding to explore mob mentality, primal urges, and the tightrope walk of animal instinct and human compassion.<br><br>Wells attempts to expand this theme by putting teenagers in a boarding school with no teachers and a sloppily constructed social order that is meted out via three groups: The Society, Havoc, and V's (the titular Variants, which was enough to make my eyes roll so far back into my skull that I could see my brainstem). Each group falls so neatly into stereotypes that it makes <i>Divergent</i>'s world-building look like poetry. <br><br>Anyway, the groups have a truce that has existed among them to maintain order in an adult-free school. The reason behind the truce is such an obvious plot device that it's pointless for me to explore its lack of depth here. Just know that it exists and it is beyond stupid. <br><br>When Benson arrives at the school, the social order begins to crumble. Why? Because Benson is a renegade. He doesn't play by the rules. <br><br>Sound familiar?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407959295i/10788284.jpg" width="300" height="250" alt="Let. Me. Spell. It. Out. For. You." class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>
  <i>Lost</i>
</b><br>J.J. Abrams' television series was compelling, fun, and slightly scary for the first season. Then as the story dragged, it became pretty apparent that the writers had painted themselves into a corner. To this day, I still haven't watched the last four seasons because I just stopped caring. From what I understand, the whole series became convoluted and culminated in a thoroughly unsatisfying series finale. <br><br>Wells follows a similar trajectory. The first hundred pages of <i>Variant</i> are filled with an endless parade of fascinating questions: Why is Benson at Maxfield Academy? Why are some of these kids acting so brainwashed? What's the meaning of the paintball wars? What's with the constant surveillance? Who is the Iceman? <br><br>(Iceman - lolz!) <br><br>As the book barrels along, though, these questions become less interesting and more frustrating. This is largely due to the fact that Benson is <i>constantly</i> asking himself these same questions, voicing the readers' curiosity with the incessant insistence of a curious 3 year-old. The more Benson wondered about his fate (which, to reiterate, is literally every chapter), the less I cared about what happened to him. By the time the "shocking" violence takes place (followed quickly by a plot twist that is hilariously awful), I had checked out entirely. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406200033ra/10518165.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="GTFO, Variant!" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>
  <i>Nearly every YA "dystopian" trope ever hewn and re-hewn and re-re-hewn ad infinitum</i>
</b><br>Seriously, YA authors. STFU. <br><br>Teens forming factions! Teens showing atypical agency and bucking the system! Teens facing an uncertain and cruel future!<br><br>This book <i>barely</i> qualifies as a "dystopia", yet it is clearly marketed as such. Its science fiction factor is at, like, .1%, and it seems to exist only because the wave of dystopian literature continues to be at an indefinite zenith. <br><br>I am <i>so</i> over this trend. After <i>The Hunger Games</i> (which I still love, but fully blame for the virtual tsunami of shit that has been on its heels), every editor in the world should have rejected the endless dystopia book pitches instead of accepting such blatant mediocrity. <br><br>I get it: publishing is a business and it's impossible not to see dollar signs. In fact, Wells was allegedly working on his Master's degree in finance while writing this book, which makes its existence seem even more... <i>calculated</i>. Buh-dum-CHING!<br><br>As a teen librarian, I know how much appeal there is to a book like <i>Variant</i>, and I will recommend the hell out of it to kids who will love its "twists", reserving, as I always do, my personal opinion and head-banging <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[about raccoons that are actually robots <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> to the comfort of my own home. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="7968389939081960806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14053011763922386863" style="display:none"><b>This was one awesome book.</b><br />I can easily say that this book was one of the most compelling reads of 2012. The blurb, the cover, the trailers, I guess everything made me read this. <br />First of all, I loved the story. After finishing "The Maze Runner" series, I was just all broken down because I adored 'The Maze Runner' trilogy and when it ended, I was so sad knowing that I won't be able to read a book like that anymore but this book just proved me wrong.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"I loved it! The twist behind it all is my favorite since ENDER'S GAMES."</b>
</i><br />-James Dashner, <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of the THE MAZE RUNNER<br /><br />So all The Maze Runner trilogy fans, this book is definitely for you.<br />I think people who rated this book 1-2 stars didn't read The Maze Runner trilogy before or are just not YA.<br />Because readers complained alot about the book being slow and that the main character is annoying, but The Maze Runner, infact every dystopian book taught me that sometimes you have to wait for the answers and the characters to develop. <br /><br />The story was really good. From the start, when Benson came to the school to adjusting till he was fighting for his life, I read this book continuously. Even though I will say, yes, the story became slow in between but then it picked up its pace and the twist in the end was just wow. I think the cover somehow gave the story away. Mainly because of the girl. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was expecting Jane to be the main heroine but the girl on the cover has brown hair and Jane has red hair so it just gave everything away. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />And readers. This is NOT a dystopian book. Donot let Goodreads fool you.<br /><br />I loved the characters too. Again Readers saying non of the characters were good and that nothing was interesting about them, well maybe they had their own reasons but for me, I loved Jane and Becky and even the Society, Variants and Havoc people. <br /><br />Overall, I will just say I loved Variant, I will rate this book 4/5 stars and I seriously NEED the next book right now.<br /><br /><i>p.s</i> Robison Wells, you wrote a book instead of learning about Finance and that was the most epic thing you have done in your life. I had an accounts test recently and I got 13/20 which was the highest. -_-</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer225255412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14186177271395608985">Okay, another book about a boarding school. Not original except there are no vampires. But, oh. It gets good. It really is different. Very different. First of all, the protagonist is a 17 year old boy. Second, the school has no teachers and the most bizarre curriculum. And it's a prison. Nobody gets out. The rules are odd and social mores are determined by a talking head on the television and the students themselves. Punishment is severe and inconsistent. Death is a real threat.<br/><br/>Benson arrives at</span>
  <span id="freeText14186177271395608985" style="display:none">Okay, another book about a boarding school. Not original except there are no vampires. But, oh. It gets good. It really is different. Very different. First of all, the protagonist is a 17 year old boy. Second, the school has no teachers and the most bizarre curriculum. And it's a prison. Nobody gets out. The rules are odd and social mores are determined by a talking head on the television and the students themselves. Punishment is severe and inconsistent. Death is a real threat.<br /><br />Benson arrives at the school and quickly wants to leave. He is approached by the leaders of the three gangs; The Society, Havocs and the Variants. In order to survive, he must choose one. Guess which one he chooses. Go ahead. Guess. They play paintball for high stakes. A prissy student teaches odd subjects dictated by someone nobody has seen. If someone is sent to detention, it can be assumed they are killed. There is blood. There are cameras and microphones. The Society are the security and the revel in their duties. Their behavior is rewarded in points which is currency. <br /><br />It just gets more and more bizarre and just when I thought I had it figured out, the author threw in a curve ball. No way. That's about the time Benson understands how precarious his position and his life really is. And then another curveball. And another. And then the ending left me with my mouth hanging open. What the crap? Not a "what the crap" stupid ending but "what the crap" I can't wait for the next book. Then being the weirdo I am, I read the acknowledgments and I realized the author lives in the same county I do.<br /><br />Dude. Don't make me stalk you. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_236799366" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/236799366" />
    <a title="Roxanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/673526-roxanne"><img alt="Roxanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1245885574p2/673526.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/236799366?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roxanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roxanne" href="/user/show/673526-roxanne">Roxanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer236799366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12103319046045865133">I will tell you, if I knew this was a "book one" I would not have bothered. I liked the read - the writing wasn't anything special and the premise was fun enough - foster kid with no family gets scholarship to special school where all the students are locked in without adults and etc etc experiments ? and big brother masterminds? and fighting and etc - I like that kind of story. And I appreciated that the main character was very WTF in an appropriate way that never stopped, and there was a cool </span>
  <span id="freeText12103319046045865133" style="display:none">I will tell you, if I knew this was a "book one" I would not have bothered. I liked the read - the writing wasn't anything special and the premise was fun enough - foster kid with no family gets scholarship to special school where all the students are locked in without adults and etc etc experiments ? and big brother masterminds? and fighting and etc - I like that kind of story. And I appreciated that the main character was very WTF in an appropriate way that never stopped, and there was a cool twist. <br /><br />But oh goddamn, another fucking cliffhanger ending. Who do I blame for this? Publishers? Like, I get it, you want to sell more books BUT YOU STILL HAVE TO FINISH THE STORY. The first Star Wars movie had a beginning, middle and end and simultaneously fit into a larger story arc AND THAT IS HOW YOU ARE SUPPOSED TO WRITE SERIES/TRILOGIES OMG KILL ME NOW.<br /><br />ALSO PLEASE LABEL BOOKS AS "BOOK ONE" AT THE VERY LEAST OMG<br /><br />Here are some alternate endings I have provided to spare your wrath:<br /><br />a) Benson and Becky escape into the woods. She scrapes herself on a log and Benson sees that she is a robot. She does not know she is a robot. He grabs her and kisses her passionately and after the kiss she smiles at him and he shoots her.<br /><br />b) Benson and Becky escape into the woods. They look for a place to camp for the night. He watches Becky tend to her wounds and thinks poetically about how strong and great she is. Suddenly, the narration cuts off and slips into different typeface. FEMALE TARGET LOCATED, it says. Benson opens his mouth and says to Becky, "YOU MUST RETURN TO SCHOOL." Becky's face falls. The end.<br /><br />c) Benson and Becky escape into the woods. They make it to the highway and flag down a truck that carries them into a nearby city. The cops don't believe them. Now she works in the market as a check out girl. She knows things will get better. He'll find work and she'll get promoted, they'll move out of the shelter and finally see what it means to be livin'. And she remembers when they were driving, driving in his car, speed so fast it felt they were drunk ... no, wait. That's a Tracy Chapman song.<br /><br />d) Benson and Becky escape into the woods. They make it to the highway and flag down a truck. The driver gives them something to eat and hurries towards the closest city. Benson and Becky are relieved. They cry and hold each other and tell the driver everything. He is outraged and so sorry for them. They both fall asleep as the truck ambles down the road and we see the drivers eyes glow. He is a robot! Suddenly we hear Vincent Price laughing, like the end of the Thriller video. <br /><br />/end scene</span>
  <a data-text-id="12103319046045865133" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_217000077" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/217000077" />
    <a title="Kaye" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4016487-kaye"><img alt="Kaye" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493585690p2/4016487.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/217000077?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaye" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaye" href="/user/show/4016487-kaye">Kaye</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of dystopian lit</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4016487-kaye?shelf=arcs-netgalley">arcs-netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4016487-kaye?shelf=2011-releases">2011-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer217000077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5526823867354123168">Now this is the type of book I've been looking for since I devoured the Shadow Children series by Margaret Peterson Haddix back in middle school. It's not a dystopian America. Benson is the type of kid you'd hear about every day, shuttled back and forth through the foster care system, getting nowhere. But unlike most down-on-their-luck little orphans, Benson doesn't look for a pair of parents for his very own, or tap-dance his way into the spotlight of some very impressed agent slash manager sla</span>
  <span id="freeText5526823867354123168" style="display:none">Now this is the type of book I've been looking for since I devoured the Shadow Children series by Margaret Peterson Haddix back in middle school. It's not a dystopian America. Benson is the type of kid you'd hear about every day, shuttled back and forth through the foster care system, getting nowhere. But unlike most down-on-their-luck little orphans, Benson doesn't look for a pair of parents for his very own, or tap-dance his way into the spotlight of some very impressed agent slash manager slash future father-in-law. He sends in for a scholarship to Maxfield Academy, a mysterious boarding school for kids like him who are down on their luck, hoping that maybe it can get his life going.<br /><br />He's right, but not in the way he thinks.<br /><br />Okay, now I must confess: for the first half of the book, I DETESTED BENSON. He sort of reminded me of Katniss (I'm sure I don't have to give a link for you to know who that is) - running against brick walls, constantly causing trouble without getting anywhere for his pains...oh yeah, and he is completely gullible when it comes to a cute girl. One thing is for sure, though, the plot wouldn't be carried off without him...and it probably wouldn't have been as fun with an infallible, all-wise and dashing hero.<br /><br />Other than the initial setback of a rather irritating protagonist, this book was completely awesome in that it never delivered exactly what you'd expect. Even the end was a cliffhanger and, although I'm not approving of series recently, I will definitely set aside my misgivings for a sequel.<br /><br />Bravo, Mr. Wells. I'm looking forward to more.<br /><br /><br />Warnings: A brief mention of exactly what teenagers are apt to think of when privacy + no adults are combined. Perhaps some language too, though I can't exactly remember at the moment. Just...proceed with caution.<br /><br />Final verdict: Yes, and eagerly awaiting more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5526823867354123168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_200131171" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/200131171" />
    <a title="Dorine White" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5268726-dorine-white"><img alt="Dorine White" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442653617p2/5268726.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/200131171?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorine White" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorine White" href="/user/show/5268726-dorine-white">Dorine White</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer200131171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2503943363440458319">Hold on to your hats! Variant, by Robinson Wells, is a ride into a young adult fantastical mystery that keeps you reading and reading. I stayed up to midnight, I couldn’t put it down. Published by HarperCollins, it runs 223 pages and is part one in a series.<br/><br/><br/>The Story- Foster child Benson Fisher wants to improve his life. He’s tired of switching homes every few months and applies for a scholarship at a prestigious private school, Maxfield Academy. He begins to doubt his good luck when he arrives </span>
  <span id="freeText2503943363440458319" style="display:none">Hold on to your hats! Variant, by Robinson Wells, is a ride into a young adult fantastical mystery that keeps you reading and reading. I stayed up to midnight, I couldn’t put it down. Published by HarperCollins, it runs 223 pages and is part one in a series.<br /><br /><br />The Story- Foster child Benson Fisher wants to improve his life. He’s tired of switching homes every few months and applies for a scholarship at a prestigious private school, Maxfield Academy. He begins to doubt his good luck when he arrives at the school, fifty miles from no where, surrounded by two huge walls, and evidently, no way out.<br /><br />His school mystery only deepens when he enters the building. There are no adults, the students rule things in gangs and teach their own classes. Plus, there are security camera’s everywhere. Benson is told the rules and warned that if he messes up bad enough, he’ll get detention, and nobody returns from detention.<br />Benson is determined to escape, but the harder he tries, the more strange information about the school comes to light. Is this some kind of strange experiment? Are the kids being trained to be super soldiers? Nothing makes sense.<br /><br />My Thoughts- I loved this book. I read so much that often books with common themes blur before my eyes. This one stood out, full of excitement that did not end. Plus, I could not figure out the mystery of the school; that alone kept me reading. If you’ve read Maze Runner by Dasher, this book is in that same vein. You spend the whole book trying to figure out the mystery, only to have it solved at the end and a whole new one put before you. Go buy this book! It totally ranks high on the creepy suspenseful scale.<br /><br />For Parents- There is violence, lots of fighting and some death. There is no sex.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.dorinewhite.blogspot.com">www.dorinewhite.blogspot.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2503943363440458319" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_243274155" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/243274155" />
    <a title="Ilsa Bick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2842442-ilsa-bick"><img alt="Ilsa Bick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468281130p2/2842442.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/243274155?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ilsa Bick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ilsa Bick" href="/user/show/2842442-ilsa-bick">Ilsa Bick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer243274155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14954579827470707253">Having been bounced around in the foster care system for years, Benson Fisher ends up at Maxfield Academy, a cloistered private school. What looks like an opportunity for this lonely, outcast kid quickly degenerates into a nightmare scenario. Maxfield Academy is a bit like a roach motel: bugs check in, but they don’t check out. There are no teachers; the kids run the classes; food and supplies are delivered via an elevator (reminiscent, actually, of The Maze Runner, whose Lord of the Flies dysto</span>
  <span id="freeText14954579827470707253" style="display:none">Having been bounced around in the foster care system for years, Benson Fisher ends up at Maxfield Academy, a cloistered private school. What looks like an opportunity for this lonely, outcast kid quickly degenerates into a nightmare scenario. Maxfield Academy is a bit like a roach motel: bugs check in, but they don’t check out. There are no teachers; the kids run the classes; food and supplies are delivered via an elevator (reminiscent, actually, of The Maze Runner, whose Lord of the Flies dystopian premise certainly informs this book); and the kids have divided up into gangs; and those kids who break the rules enough to warrant “detention” never return. It was a fun-enough scenario to get me interested, and the book’s pacing was just great . . .<br /> <br />Until I hit a major reveal that happens about, oh, halfway through the book, I think. It was such a jarring and unexpected reveal that I actually stopped reading because there really wasn’t much in the way of clues or preparation. The thing felt as if it came out of the blue, a little like bringing in the aliens. It really is a deus ex machina moment, literally. There’s just no getting around that.<br /> <br />But I let myself simmer down, and then instead of chucking the book, I just did a mental shrug and kept going. The book is a fun, fast read and if it were not for that stumble, I wouldn’t have any problems with this at all. While I saw the final plot twists and end coming, that didn’t keep me from reading right up until the end either. So, if you can get past the big reveal–and I’d encourage you to–you won’t be sorry. I’ll be interested to see where the sequel goes with this.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14954579827470707253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_194846964" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3909637-michelle-madow?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>,
